Post #1  (forum post #531564)
Author    : Laser Brain
Date      : Mar 10, 2008 at 3:17 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hi guys,

I've set myself the task of trying to build a studio scale Tydirium. Thing is, I can only work on it one day a week and I have eight weeks to finish it. Therefore, it is unlikely to be 100% accurate, but I'm going to try and get it as close as I can.

I have some of the kits that I need (Leopold, Morser Karl, 20mm Flakvierling, 1:20 F1 Tyrell, Tamiya 1/35 (8Rad) Sdkfz 232) but don't rcognise anything else on the model.

This is the end of week one (day one). I have built and partially detailed the dorsal wing. The side wings have been partially built and detailed.

[IMAGE: 6650590.jpeg]

[IMAGE: 6689041.jpeg]

[IMAGE: 6709996.jpeg]

Cheers

Neil

Looks like a great start so far! 

BUT may i ask why you are in such a 'hurry' in building this baby? I mean, setting up such a relatively close schedule (about 8 days) for a project like this, will probably result in a good number of compromises. 

And as you are even going to use authentic kit parts, it would be a pity not to go the Dead-On-Route. 

Especially since there is a good amount of ref-pics from diverse exhibits. 

Don't get me wrong - just my thoughts...

It's so nice to see someone do an accurate Imp Shuttle!

I used to adore the Airfix kit that came out late '83, but could never figure out why the cockpit was so drooped down.....i later realised they must have used the pics/blueprints of the partial full size shuttle which has a distinctly nose down quality when compared to the ILM miniatures.

......seemed to have rambled on a wee bit......

Kudos on some stunning work sir!

Rich

Click to expand...

 

Hey Neil, awesome job so far !

Do you plan to motorize the wings and light the model ?

Be careful bout the kitparts though, some (like the flak38 shields) were copied and scratchbuilt at a bigger scale, so if you use them on your model they will be too small or if you used them to scale up your model, your model will be too small.

Cant wait to see more ! 8 weeks will be very short ! Good luck :thumbsup
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Author    : Laser Brain

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

The wing armature is made from a medium density styling board - the same type I used to make my Roadster patterns. I am trying to use only my left over materials.

N

Post #20  (forum post #534232)
Author    : Laser Brain
Date      : Mar 13, 2008 at 12:56 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hi guys,

I found a little time this afternoon to work on the shuttle.

I found some Tamiya German 20mm Flak38 (MIT Sd.Ah.51) parts that I used to scale up part of the side wings. I still need to refine some of the edges and identify the remaining part for this panel. It looks like some kind of tow rope spool. I'm not sure.

[IMAGE: 7593321.jpeg]

I started detailing the front recess of the dorsal wing too with what I believe are the correct parts (Morser Karl and Tamiya 20mm FLAKVIERLING): 

[IMAGE: 7739546.jpeg]

I don't currently have any reference for the top. My reference for the rear is mostly in shadow. I'm going to have to leave those blank for the time being.

The 'cog' parts for the wing mechanism will be laser cut next week along with an acrylic internal support structure for the body which will also house part of the mech and batteries. 

N

Post #24  (forum post #535015)
Author    : Laser Brain
Date      : Mar 14, 2008 at 12:49 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hey, thanks guys.

REL very kindly uploaded a load of great reference for me and I have realised that wanting to complete this model as quickly as I do just isn't realistic. I am going to have to dedicate more time to this. Some late nights are in order. I have noticed that the panels on my wings are too thick. I'm going to have to live with that until after my show.

Anyway, I made a section of the body this afternoon. The vacforming patterns are polyurethane foam. I used 1.5mm styrene:

[IMAGE: 23.jpg]

Here it is primed and double-sided to the dorsal wing.

 

[IMAGE: 25.jpg]

 

[IMAGE: 26.jpg]

 

[IMAGE: 24.jpg]

I don't suppose anyone has a koolshade off-cut they want to sell ;-)

Hi guys. Thanks a lot. I did a little bit more on it today.

The structure for the main body has been laser cut. It will be held together with 19.1mm (don't ask!) brass tubing:

[IMAGE: 7124576.jpeg]

...as have the parts for the wing mech. I dropped these into rubber just before I left to come home for the day. I'll be casting them up tomorrow and joining them to the side wings:

[IMAGE: 7257928.jpeg]

Cheers

Neil

Post #118  (forum post #555271)
Author    : Laser Brain
Date      : Apr 11, 2008 at 12:17 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hi guys. I'm not sure when the Tydirium will be available. I haven't started the patterns yet!!
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 Also, I won't be doing the moulding/casting. Somebody much more experienced has offered. It will happen though.

I identified what I believe to be the parts that make the 4 major details on the dorsal wing. There is still a little part that sits at the rear of each of these that I will add tomorrow (from the flakvierling I think) :

[IMAGE: 0552905.jpeg]

Added some more correct parts where the 'neck' joins the body:

[IMAGE: 0849411.jpeg]

I need your opinions on this too. I no longer plan to light v1. I don't have the time, and to be honest the lighting kinda slipped my mind when I assembled the main body, making a clean, quick and trouble free installation nothing more than a fantasy.:$ So, I made this for the rear engines:

[IMAGE: 1011072.jpeg]

I drew it up last night and had it laser cut in 1.5mm and 3mm acrylic. Bear in mind, it will be dark and weathered. I just can't face looking at a neon bulb or some EL strip. What do you think?

Here it is in situ:

[IMAGE: 1087457.jpeg]

Cheers

Post #137  (forum post #558869)
Author    : Laser Brain
Date      : Apr 16, 2008 at 11:42 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hi guys. Before I tackle the cockpit I wanted to finish as much of the fuselage and wings as I could. I originally thought the air intakes were from a 1:24 Harrier, perhaps two joined together to create a longer intake, using the 3 bands to hide a join? I tried this and it still looked slightly too small for my model. 

[IMAGE: 0312516.jpeg]

So, I vacformed what I had made so it enlarged by 3mm in height and 1.5mm in depth. It seems to have worked OK. I just need to remove the little curve in the fuselage where it meets the front of the air intake, and tweak the angle of the intake slightly.

[IMAGE: 0626033.jpeg]

[IMAGE: 0756669.jpeg]

[IMAGE: 0779835.jpeg]

I have also joined the engine shroud to the rear of the fuselage. Still needs cleaning up though.

[IMAGE: 0803213.jpeg]

N

Post #176  (forum post #563344)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Apr 22, 2008 at 9:12 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

steveo said:

			Please don't take this the wrong way, but to me, your version seems to resemble the Kenner toy with its proportions than the actual SS model that I'm used to seeing.
		

Click to expand...

Steveo, I think Vos has about nailed it. Have a look at this pic of the original. 

The Kenner toy was really quite accurate by the way. It's almost the same size and has pretty good proportions - MUCH better than the MPC plastic kit. Unlike the kit, it was mastered from drawings and photographs of the original model. 

Sadly, the plastic kit proportions (and a couple of the matte paintings in the film, too) were derived from photos and drawings of the set mockup. The mockup blueprints were drawn in Britain by UK draughtsmen from non-orthographic photos of the ILM model, which is why it doesn't match very well.

Vos, I have about another 160 pics if you can use 'em.

Cheers,

Martyn

Post #199  (forum post #566054)
Author    : mverta

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

vaderdarth said:

			Vos,  do me a favor and shoot your model about 3 feet away looking down at an angle that centers the area between the fin and the top of the cockpit................Try to keep the whole model in the photo.  I think that will illustrate whether the cockpit length from nose to rear is spot on or not.  Some of the pics of the prop seem to suggest that it's longer than this one........but I believe it's just an illusion.  I think this will answer that .

Dave 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Click to expand...

Unless you're matching filmback and focal length, this will not answer anything reliably, because the distortions (thence proportions) won't be equal.  There are ways to solve these issues photogrammetrically if you have enough of the right photo references, though. You have to correlate multiple photos together to obtain a virtual camera model, and then you can reverse engineer the true dimensions from that.  I do it all the time for accident re-creations.

_Mike
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #297  (forum post #685129)
Author    : Laser Brain
Date      : Oct 3, 2008 at 10:06 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hey guys,

I've just spent the week working on the v2 at the university workshop. I was able to rent some space there before the new term starts.

[IMAGE: 3012868.jpeg]

The upper fuselage part (in yellow) is a new sculpt, slightly longer than the v1, to fit the longer lower fuselage. The slope of the koolshade grill is also slightly changed. The upper fuselage section slots into the lower section and it locked in place by the sloped parts below the intakes. The intakes have a less 'up-and-down' profile now. The cockpit is a little slimmer in places, but only just, with more curve in the nose. The 'ears' are closer together too.

[IMAGE: 3041420.jpeg]

All the wings are larger, especially the side wings. They made in the same way however, polyurethane foam core with styrene skins. The front and back recessed areas will be cut from the wings and cast separately. The neck is considerably narrower.

Cheers

Neil

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Thanks people.
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 And Lee, I'm really looking forward to seeing how people will approach the build of these too, once they are complete.

Here is an update for you guys:

The dorsal wing is almost done and has been chopped up. I have almost completed the recessed details too - just waiting for a couple of kits to arrive and it'll be there.

[IMAGE: 5301281.jpeg]

Same goes for the swing wings:

[IMAGE: 5323790.jpeg]

I still need to start the rear of the fuselage but the rest of it is pretty much there. Again, I am waiting on kits for this:

[IMAGE: 5371781.jpeg]

Cockpit is almost done too. I just need to complete the details on the side panels:

[IMAGE: 5355454.jpeg]

Post #364  (forum post #725080)
Author    : Laser Brain
Date      : Nov 26, 2008 at 3:39 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Thanks Julien. This one is definitely better than v1. I still have much to learn about this model. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

As I will not be doing the moulding/casting for lights, I can't say what the exact plan is yet, but the wings will be cast with internal metal rods/sections for wires and anti-sag.

I'd love to see someone do one with landing gear that lowered as the wings moved upward. All in aluminium. It won't be in the one I do for myself though (unless someone makes a bunch and I snag one). Hint. Someone? 

Some more pics. Test-fitting and checking I haven't done something stupid.

[IMAGE: 1320507.jpeg]

The rear gun surround will be cast at a separate plate that fits over the rear face of the upper fuselage hollow casting. There is plenty of space behind the gun to mount the model from the rear with an internal armature.

[IMAGE: 1541075.jpeg]

Random pic. Drilling guides in the patterns for rod that slides through the gear shaped wing gizmos. 

[IMAGE: 1673615.jpeg]

Neil

Post #415  (forum post #796132)
Author    : REL
Date      : Feb 14, 2009 at 8:09 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Neil has asked me to make the shuttle kits for him. 

I got the ship today, everything arrived undamaged, it's really huge and extremely detailed and well put together. I'll post pics of the master later today. 

I was planning on trying to make this completely out of resin, but after seeing the size, I think it would be best if the main body were fiberglass. Luckily since none of it has to be clear I can use a faster setting, stronger and lighter fiberglass composite. Something that won't take a week to lay up.

I'll have to wait to see what it's actually going to take to mold and cast it to see how much they'll cost. 

Also, I can't take pre-orders, they will go out as they're made.

Post #432  (forum post #796653)
Author    : REL
Date      : Feb 14, 2009 at 9:09 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Sorry guys, but this thing is huge, and very detailed, meaning it will go through molds fast. And since it's going to be a mixed medium of fiberglass and resin, it's going to be very expensive to produce. A support structure will have to be cast into the wings so they'll remain straight. 

Of course I could make the whole thing out of resin, but then you'd end up with something that weighed 10 pounds and would be very hard to light. 

I called several kit producers today asking what they would charge, and my estimate was based on that, actually on the low side of that estimate. 

I went through this same thing before when I first released my Ent E, undercharging for it because people complained at my first price, which I now regret because it turns out I was making them at a loss. 

You guys will not be happy with the price of the Slave. :eek
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #453  (forum post #799110)
Author    : Spiker
Date      : Feb 17, 2009 at 10:41 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Only thing to complain for me is that the project left europe because that means very high shipping as well as custom fees for us europeans.

The 875 to 1000 seem absolutly reasonalbe for me. Problem would be the roundabout 150$ shipping + 300 customs and tax.

So in the end a european (in this case german) buyer ends up with 1450$ (estimated sales price 1000$ for the kit) getting this from the US instead of 1050$ getting it from the UK. As you see this is nearly half of the salesprice for the complete kit (just for um... eh... nothing..).

Maybe REL can ship the european bunch as a whole to VOS and he does the sales for europe. I guess shipping all together is much more effective an costs less.

Post #492  (forum post #813982)

Date      : Mar 7, 2009 at 8:42 AM

Yes, the whole kit will be designed for lighting. 

I've had to modify a few parts to make it so, like hollowing out a few parts that were filled with foam, then reinforcing them on the inside with a brace.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #493  (forum post #814151)
Author    : REL
Date      : Mar 7, 2009 at 1:42 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I learn something new every day.

Taking Frank's suggestion about "buttering" the mold, I used an old two piece mold from the 1/350 K'tinga and laid fiberglass in both sides, let it cure, then mixing cabosil and epoxy fiberglass, ran a thin bead on either side of the edge, then clamped the mold together letting it set up. When I pulled the mold, I had a hollow fiberglass casting. 

Here's the piece next to a solid resin casting. 

[IMAGE: ss_ty_006.jpg]

And cut in half to show that it's hollow.

[IMAGE: ss_ty_004.jpg]

So I made the mold for the main body so it's keyed, and can be clamped together after each side has fiberglass laid in. So when it's done, there will be no gluing, sanding etc. on the fiberglass part. When it's build, you'll have to cut access panels in for lighting and the armature. 

[IMAGE: ss_ty_005.jpg]

I think I'm going to use this same technique on a lot of things in the future, like the studio scale Defiant for instance.

Here's the first casting of the upper structure, this is resin. I had to make a few modifications to Neil's part so it could be more hollow. 

I've decided to make the wings out of hollow fiberglass, I think resin will be too heavy in the long run, and since the wings will be hollow lighting will be easier, plus with fiberglass they should be light enough to allow for motorization if someone is so inclined. 

Thanks

Post #525  (forum post #820196)
Author    : REL
Date      : Mar 15, 2009 at 7:22 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Sorry, I thought I got everyone. PM sent.

To answer the questions about the casting, you have to make a two piece mold, and make lots of vent holes, and pour the resin from the backside of the mold instead of the top. It won't work any other way with a thin edge like that.

Of course it makes a little more work to remove all the sprues that are left.

And you have to use very slow setting resin, I used Smooth Cast 310 with a 2 hour demold time.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #542  (forum post #823202)
Author    : REL
Date      : Mar 18, 2009 at 5:50 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Well it dried a lot faster than I thought, and it came out about 90% perfect. There's a few bubbles in the lay up, but they're under the surface and don't break through. Other than that, I'm very happy with the results. For lighting I'll have to cut access panels on the top, but that will be much easier than having to glue the two fiberglass halves together.

It's hard to see the detail, so I tried to take the pics at an angle. 

This whole piece weighs 14 oz and it's very strong. Much much lighter than if I went with resin or rotocast. 

[IMAGE: ss_ty_015.jpg]

[IMAGE: ss_ty_016.jpg]

[IMAGE: ss_ty_017.jpg]

Post #589  (forum post #861678)
Author    : REL
Date      : May 2, 2009 at 1:43 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I tried rotocasting the main body today and it tured out better than I could have imagined. I'm still going to make the top wing fiberglass, because I don't think it would be a good idea to have that much weight resting on top, but if I continue to make the main body fiberglass it will take about 2 years to get all these out. 

Body mold in homemade rotocaster.

[IMAGE: ss_ty_027.jpg]

Main body parts next to the SS Slave for size comparison.

[IMAGE: ss_ty_025.jpg]

Close up of casting

Post #596  (forum post #874127)
Author    : REL
Date      : May 15, 2009 at 4:25 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I have the wings molded now. 

I cast them by brushing in one layer of resin, then backing it with fiberglass, then after that dries, brushing fiberglass resin along the seam, clamping the mold together, and it comes out hollow and lightweight. 

This huge wing weighs hardly anything. 

[IMAGE: ss_ty_028.jpg]

I'm doing all the wings this way so they'll all be hollow.

Post #625  (forum post #883892)
Author    : REL
Date      : May 26, 2009 at 7:16 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Neil that build up is just incredible!

For those getting the kit, you'll need to buy 3/4" aluminum rod for the wing hinges, you can get that at Ace Hardware here in the states, get about a 2 foot length. You'll also need a dremel with a cutting wheel, preferably with a snake attachment, and a flat ******* file for the hinge openings, they're not open on the kit, so you'll have to cut them out and file them straight. 

I'll start posting pics of the build up I'm doing tomorrow, my camera battery died today so I couldn't take any.

I'm going to start casting these now as fast as I can.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #626  (forum post #884645)

Post #627  (forum post #884814)
Author    : REL
Date      : May 27, 2009 at 3:10 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Neil, since yours looks exactly like the studio model, all I can do is hope to copy you. :lol

I'm starting the build now. To run the wiring from the lower wings, you'll have to drill a hole in the wing hinge, then through the aluminum tube, leavingt enough slack for the full rotation of the wings, so you'll have enough wire to run it into your power supply. I'm using a flasher circuit I got from James Roberts, the timing is perfect for the shuttle while watching ROTJ last night.

[IMAGE: ss_ty_build_01.jpg]

Since the main hull is rotocast, you'll have to cut an access panel in the top, don't worry, that will be covered up by the upper hull.

[IMAGE: ss_ty_build_02.jpg]

[IMAGE: ss_ty_build_03.jpg]

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Thank you kindly everyone.

I've decided to make the wings pure fiberglass with not resin brush coat at all. Mainly for weight, these are super light, and a little more hollow since it's thinner. And that's a big plus when you're trying to snake the wiring through for the lights. 

This set here is for Guy Cowen.

Post #700  (forum post #930385)
Author    : REL
Date      : Jul 13, 2009 at 3:42 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

vaderdarth said:

			How do you do the clear canopy?
		

Click to expand...

I put bluetape over the window, cutting it perfectly to shape... 

[IMAGE: ss_ty_build_16.jpg]

...then took the tape off in one piece, laid it on a piece of thin clear styrene, using it as a guide to cut out the window, cutting it a little larger so I could fine tune it,  then using a hair dryer (a heat gun was too hot and warped it) slowly bent it to shape. 

It took about 3 tries to get it right. After I got it the right shape, I painted the back of the glass flat black.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #712  (forum post #933323)
Author    : Laser Brain
Date      : Jul 16, 2009 at 2:10 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Great news Rich. You've done a fantastic job moulding the patterns.

To make the clear canopy you could try cutting out the resin screen to use  as a guide to form the clear styrene over, using the hairdryer. Make the new screen slightly larger/longer, spray the reverse black and mount from inside the cockpit. 

Neil

Post #713  (forum post #938816)
Author    : Guy Cowen
Date      : Jul 22, 2009 at 10:10 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Well, what can I say? I received 2 Shuttle kits today from Rich. Here is a mini review upon first inspection, I'll be as honest as I can as I haven't laid all the parts out yet as I've only just walked through the door.

I'm going to start with the negatives as this doesn't deserve to end on bad news, hold your hats??/

Neg: 

1. sadly there are no instructions with the Kit, but I'm guessing that these will be available very soon.

2.Some small details on the underside of the hull where damaged in transit, they are V small greebee's that just didn't take the journey & it was the same with both kits, a real shame but also a minor problem, I'll let Rich no asap so he can avoid it on any others.   Thats it.

Pos:

This is by far the best casting I have ever seen, It is way better than any GK I have owned & even better than the F&M E wing which was top class all the way.

The detail is incredible, Neil & rich have done an incredible job on this beast. The wings are as straight as a die. 

The clear resin engine parts are almost works of art & you would never in a million years think they are from a GK.

There really isn't anything bad to say about this at all, I know I still need to go through the bags of smaller parts but I am blown away already. Having just spent 2 months of my life cleaning up a Y wing & B wing it makes it an absolute pleasure to see such craftsmanship. 

The only way to improve this would be on the presentation of the kit, I think it will be a long time before anyone presents a kit as well as F&M models if Rich took a leaf from there book, ie: check list, instructions, packing (although the packing was good with the shuttles) it would be the most pro GK ever produced. 

Rich, Neil, thanks so much for getting this off the ground & into our hands It really is stunning work. Let me know if there is a pdf of the instructions as although it does seem simple enough, you cant beat a bit of help? 

My recommendation..........      Buy one NOW! Its worth every penny

I also got my Lee Ralph Mastered PD pod but I'll post that in the appropriate thread.

A few air bubbles that have ruined some smaller parts (I'll add pics later) & a few warped pieces that are possibly salvageable, most of the gun barrels will need to be replaced with brass or alu, it will be quicker to make new ones than straighten the parts supplied. Sorry about the lack of pics but I'm unpacking from being away & trying to be domestic at the same time.  Still an amazing Kit, I'd give it 97.5/100. Pics shortly.

Post #717  (forum post #939053)
Author    : REL
Date      : Jul 22, 2009 at 2:16 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Guy, 

Thanks for the review, I apologize for the parts that didn't make it out ok.  I was sure I inspected each part but apparently I missed a few. Also thanks for the heads up on the bodies, I'll wrap the next one's that go out in bubble wrap or something to protect them better, I thought they would make it ok with the packing I did, but I guess I was wrong. 

The guns, I nearly just sent brass tubes cut for the guns as I figured no one would use the resin ones, (I didn't use them on my build) but at least you can use them as a guide to make the metal one's. 

Just let me know which parts aren't satisfactory and I can send out replacements free of charge.

Post #748  (forum post #1147618)
Author    : swpropmaker
Date      : Mar 3, 2010 at 1:06 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

“Command Station…This is ST 321 Code Clearance Blue..” 

Studio Scale Tydirium Shuttle

Hey guys.. it’s time to deactivate the security shield…. The Shuttle Tydirium V3 is starting it’s approach.  I’ve taken over the wonderful patterns made by our very own Neil aka VOS!  First run of kit by REL….. The patterns are fantastic!  

[IMAGE: 383659195.jpg]

However there are some part accuracy problems on the original build. Though the original scratched parts are dead on…. Neil suggested I upgrade prior to the next release.  

 Ive spent the last couple months getting this puppy more accurate with original kit parts!  So here are some of the pictures

First I hollowed out an area for the Koolshade to go.  The original pattern this area was filled in.  Once the casting is made the section of Koolshade will be glue in from the back side.

[IMAGE: 383659178.jpg]

 

[IMAGE: 383659155.jpg]

 

[IMAGE: 383659166.jpg]

[IMAGE: 383659150.jpg]

Once this was complete I found parts to upgrade the guns and lower hulls with accurate details.

[IMAGE: 383659246.jpg]

[IMAGE: 383659236.jpg]

[IMAGE: 383659228.jpg]

 

I was informed that the detail cluster on back of the head was scratched so I replaced those parts with accurate version to the studio model.  I created a two part head pattern.   I had to add about 2cm of material to the overall head to make room for the original parts. I also opened up the upper cockpit to allow room for a cockpit. 

[IMAGE: 383659217.jpg]

 

[IMAGE: 383659208.jpg]

 

[IMAGE: 383659212.jpg]

 

[IMAGE: 383659223.jpg]

 

[IMAGE: 383659254.jpg]

 

On a side note.. Neils patterns are so size accurate the original parts dropped in place without much reworking!!  Great Job Neil!

The last upgrade was to the lower nose detail… I added the 4 correct scoops.

[IMAGE: 383659250.jpg]

 

[IMAGE: 383659274.jpg]

The shuttle will also come with 6 laser cut acrylic gears.  The wings will not be hollow epoxy but rather stock aluminum reinforced resin.  The stock will not allow any movement.  As in all my hero models there will be an aluminum armature available as well as a light kit produced by VooDoo FX.   I’m in the molding stage now.  

Rich sent me his interest list but I had a computer crash and lost this information.  I’ve got phone calls and emails into Rich to see if he still has this..  if not and you  want to know more info shoot me a pm or better yet an email  sneisen@bresnan.net

I will post pictures of the castings as soon as they are complete..  will also start an interest list in the Junk Yard!

Thanks for looking!

Steve

Post #761  (forum post #1150786)
Author    : REL
Date      : Mar 6, 2010 at 2:06 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I think I figured out the easiest way to paint this. 

I put on a coat of Plastikote black sandable primer, lacquer (I've tried several combinations of rattle can primers, and the lacquers seem to work the best)

anyway, black primer on first, like 3 coats. Then, Plastikote white sandable primer over that, one wet coat only, not a dust coat. 

It gives you a nice super light grey with dark undertones.

[IMAGE: ty_build_21.jpg]

Then for the weathering detail, use a light cream color for some earth tones sprayed into the deeper recesses , with super thinned black for the darker weathering. 

[IMAGE: ty_build_20.jpg]

Credit for this find goes to pro kit part hunter and scratch builder Big John Curilla..  John said he was going through known used ROTj kits (donor for AT-St) and found the Shuttle jack pot... the kit has 8 parts.  the kit you seek is the 1/32 Tamiya F-14 Tomcat

Thanks againt to John and Neil for the opportunity to re release this kit in all its accurate glory!

Steve

Post #789  (forum post #1162212)
Author    : Mattax487
Date      : Mar 18, 2010 at 12:10 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

REL said:

			I put bluetape over the window, cutting it perfectly to shape... 

[IMAGE: ss_ty_build_16.jpg]

...then took the tape off in one piece, laid it on a piece of thin clear styrene, using it as a guide to cut out the window, cutting it a little larger so I could fine tune it,  then using a hair dryer (a heat gun was too hot and warped it) slowly bent it to shape. 

It took about 3 tries to get it right. After I got it the right shape, I painted the back of the glass flat black.
		

Click to expand...

WOW! I'm probably echoing everyone else here, but this is the first time I have seen this. Truly amazing. And thanks for the info on making the window.

Post #873  (forum post #1559686)
Author    : Skyjedi
Date      : Feb 17, 2011 at 1:55 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Waited for 7 months, which is 2 years ago for the kit and begging for 1 year for the missing parts.  I have finally received my missing parts from Richard. I am a bit more lucky then some of the folks here, that I did get the kit.  Finally I can start to build.  Unfortunately the kit was poorly casted, airpockets all over the kit, after putting the wings together the gaps needs to be heavily filled with resins.  Guns are extremely fragile, they also needed to be replaced by metal tubing.  

It's not a lost that you have not purchased the kit, the original builder Neil had done such a amazing job on the shuttle, it's a shame that it's ruined by the mold makers.  (I'm sure the ones they cast for themselves was excellent, but the ones for sell...... no quality control)

For the folks who are considering buying kits from builders on this site, I strongly suggest you to reconsider.  From my personal first time shopping experience on this site, it has given me only frustration and disappointment, nothing else.  They will receive your $$ and you have no security, no garantee and protection that it will be shipped to you.  If they don't, you can't really chase for refund.  

Unless you really know the builder well or you have sources to find them personally, otherwise buying here is like buying luck.  Just what Neil mentioned above "GOOD LUCK"!!!!!!

Michael,

I've ordered the kit from Richard in Jun 2009, promised to deliver the kit in 3 months period, after chasing finally received in end Dec 2009.  Unfortunately found out some major parts missing, contacted him for the replacement.  Unfortunately no reply for a long time.  Until got really upset with him, he finally replied and told me he doesn't have the mold anymore, needs to find the mold to remake the missing parts.  After waited and waited, no reply from him, I ask for advice on the forum, Neil suggested me to contact Steve for the missing parts.  Steve replied and told me to send him my address, he will send me the missing parts, unfortunately after sending my address, he disappeared.  

Another few months went by, before giving up, I noticed Richard is still very active on this forum and talks about his new build Snow Speeder.  I send him another message stating that he's got so much time to build his snow speeder but why doesn't have time to help to get the missing parts.  He finally replied and says he will use his own kit to cast the missing parts.  (Why he told me he doesn't have the mold in the first place?)  

Finally received the missing parts after a few months time which is end of Jan 2011.  Imagine all the hassles that I need to went through to just get the complete kit.

I wish you all the luck with Richard and "May The Force Be With the folks who's still waiting for the missing kits from the irresponsible model builders....."

Post #883  (forum post #1563512)
Author    : hugescale
Date      : Feb 20, 2011 at 1:28 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Skyjedi,

I would like to tell you what is going on with the kits I have ordered from Richard. Unfortunately I can not.

I have received changing information over the past years. A lot of them are contradictory. OK, there is one constant message saying "Hang in there, you will receive great kits".

The only thing I know for sure ist that I paid for 2 Tydirium kits in May 2009 and for 2 K´tingas kits in October 2007 and that I am still waiting.

Jedi Date,

Regarding quality, I have received several y-wing kits from Steve. Especially the bodies are absolutely super and the best resin parts I have received so far.

A long time ago, I have received 3 tie kits from Steve. Due to delays, I started pushing him to get moving and to sent me the kits. I have received soft castings from worn out molds with a lot of details missing. The wings were absolutely flat. So I thought that when using the details from two kits for the third one, I can build a nice model. About two years ago I had those parts in my hands again. I deceided, that is not worth putting that huge amount of time into the kits. The details would be replaced, but they still would be very very soft.  Selling them was not an option, because I did not wanted to upset a potential buyer. Bottom line is, that they ended up in the garbage can. I have learned from that experience, that pushing can result in a bad result.

As for my experience with Richard regarding quality: I have received a concept x-wing kit in an absolutey fantastic quality from him. We agreed that I will pay for it once once the outstanding kits are ready to ship.

So there is still hope.

Michael

Post #884  (forum post #1563663)
Author    : CutThumb
Date      : Feb 20, 2011 at 7:04 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

If people expect to get repeat business for these kits from customers , which are both terribly time consuming to mold and produce, the bottom line is they must deliver the kits. There are a lot of new people joining this site who want to buy and build these models yet don't have a clue  about who is providing them. Three years ago I didn't know , it took me six months to find out and I 'm still learning and I went entirely by word of mouth and was pretty happy from whom I bought from until recently. 

 There is little to no information about the vendors other than by whats posted up on these and other forums  by  those who have dealt with them, and I ask ,how can you build a strong business  and reputation if you don't provide what you say you will ? Nobody is going to fork out  any money to sellers who obviously don't deliver what they promise? There are about five kits that I still want for myself in the SW universe that are out there or being made . I had one near miss that was solved by another molder taking over.  

  And we are not talking small amounts of money here. Anyone  reading Skyjedis and hugescales stories has got to feel for them and newbies will never take the risk based on a purchase based on what they've said. So sellers won't shift the kits and they won't make any money on the few they do. Its a vicious circle and the end result will be nobody benefits at all and the businesses are killed dead and this hobby will suffer for it. There are afterall only so many scale models out there in the starwars galaxy.

 As a guide between shipping notification and reciept dates outside of the US, in the UK  I've had most kits in under fifteen days (eight being the best so far). Anything over thirty I'd question. 

  And its becoming obvious that the longer this goes on the more likely it is people will keep bumping these threads up so they get read and more damage is done to the seller until the problems are solved. A single dispute from one buyer won't draw much attention but several?

   I will happily promote anyone who deals fairly and squarely and be as fair as I can be with the product I recieve and hopefull,as a result,  help them grow their business as well. I'm all for a win/win situation. But the problem will be that if a few continue not to met their obligations to customers then they will ruin the trade by simple association and the places they frequent. God knows why they don't get help from other experienced people on these boards who seem more than willing to step up to the mark and assist. In these times of unemployment and tight cash flows I'd have thought it better to keep your constant customers on your side rather than alienate them and risk sinking a business.

  Happily it appears that people have taken action now and huge inroads are being made into the outstanding orders lists. This is in no small part to some of the very experienced guys in this forum who have stepped forward ,organised things and taken up the challenge. The results are very good to say the least , and its a credit to everyone involved that things have moved forward the way they have done.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #885  (forum post #1563953)
Author    : REL
Date      : Feb 20, 2011 at 12:00 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I have no excuses that I can give for this. It's obvious by now that I'm a horrible business man. I got way over my head in this business, at first not charging enough, getting behind, not being realistic with my time lines or costs on these projects,  then having to make new projects to pay for old ones, then getting behind on those as well. I can't remember the last time I did a project and was able to invest the money in that project, instead of having to buy supplies for old ones. 

People are upset that I sell new stuff when I owe old, I don't do that out of a sense of greed or dishonesty, but simply to buy more resin.

People ask for exact dates when I can ship their stuff, at this point I have no idea. I work on these things daily and send stuff out when I can, with the help of other casters and myself. I can understand how no one wants to hear that.

I'm in no way blaming the people that ordered from me, so please don't take it that way. I truly appreciate that you ordered from me, and very sorry that you're now waiting for something you paid for so long ago. 

If it's any consolation, I'm no longer in the kit business and will not be making any new kits, or taking new orders on any of my existing kits. The orders that I have now will be the last ones. Once I'm caught up this will all become a hobby to me again, not for business, except to sell completed build ups for just one or two clients. The kit masters I have that are caught up are either destroyed, sold or given away so I won't be tempted to offer kits for sale again. Kit production is by far the most expensive and time consuming part, for me, of this business, by eliminating that I can now focus on my backlog and get everyone caught up, and satisfy everyone I owe. 

I'm not going to leave, or bolt, or take your money and run. By getting out of the thing that has caused me to become so behind, kits, will be a big step in making sure that I can get caught up and not just add to my backlog.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #887  (forum post #1564146)
Author    : Primetime21
Date      : Feb 20, 2011 at 2:55 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

It's not hard at all.  You have to investigate and understand the hobby.  The first thing I wanted to do when I got into the GK business was to improve on that which seems to plague this industry.  Poor customer service, not responding to emails and sending out a product which is sub-standard.

The one thing you have to understand as a GK'er is that the minute you took money from someone for a product you became a business.  I've seen all of the excuses...life happens, it's just a hobby, thats all well and good but you still have peoples money.  I have a system in place in case something were to happen to me people would still get their kits.  Then again, I don't take money unless I have the kit in hand.  If everybody would adopt a similar business practice these things could be avoided.

With that said, I commend Richard for coming on and beiing honest.  Good job buddy!

My two cents.

Author    : swpropmaker
Date      : Dec 13, 2011 at 3:03 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hey Simon,

Yeah.. model design not changed but material has.  The resin switch has made a 100% improvement.. leaving the Poly Tek Easy flo series to Smooth on 300 series products.  The wings are cast in Smooth on 310 and the other parts in Smooth On 300.  Same products Mike Salzo uses..  I'm planning to have a couple shuttles poured and tested by Christmas..  hopefully the kit becomes stable and does not move around..  that would be a good thing!

Steve

Post #932  (forum post #2751444)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Feb 16, 2013 at 1:26 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Johno said:

			A question about the full scale made on the set of Return of the jedi. Was that scale destroyed after the film? http://www.dvdactive.com/editorial/articles/star-wars-the-changes-part-two.html?page=4

Click to expand...

All the large sound stage sets were struck after filming (there are pics of the remains of X-wings and the second Falcon on the back lot). The only things left in situ were the Tunisian constructions, AFAIK.

The shuttle in the shot Nazgul posted is mostly a matte painting. Several of the shots of these shuttles landed are mattes or partly mattes. One of them (Endor landing platform - Pangrazio I think?) was based on the filming model but this one is based around the mockup - easy to tell, since the proportions of the mockup were visibly different to those of the main filming model. (The MPC kit has the same mockup/matte painting proportions.)
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #938  (forum post #2765928)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Feb 24, 2013 at 6:33 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Johno...Lucas forgive you? That model is the reference standard from which everything else is derived. The mockup and the mattes came after the model, and are based on blueprints drawn from photos of the model. So if LFL took the approach that the model is the prime reference, why shouldn't you? 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #939  (forum post #2766764)
Author    : Johno
Date      : Feb 24, 2013 at 3:59 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I try to stay with reference from one scale model as it can be easy to get confused when using two or more. Especially when we don't realize we're looking at different models 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 Luckily thanks to your awesome photos in this case that won't happen. Making an amalgamation of two different scales will mean I won't be making an exact replica of either and have been persecuted in the past for doing so. But when I find more details on the full scale that are not on any of the other scales ( example the ramp way ) I think not adding those details would be a pity. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #940  (forum post #2775663)
Author    : Johno
Date      : Feb 28, 2013 at 11:43 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hmmmmmmmm I've come up against a bit of a snag involving the cockpit area. I have used the models measurements to create the shape of the exterior of the cockpit but it appears to be almost double the width we see in the movie when looking at the interior. I have placed six 6ft tall dummies in there to help attain proportions and looking at the images from the movie I have 2 different versions.

The movie image has Han and Chewie driving, with 2 seats behind them for Luke and leia and more space behind them for R2 and 3PO to stand. It sounds like a big room and looks very cramped in the image we see. ( actually I think chewie complains about the lack of space haha ) But even with room for 6 bodies and the chairs they sit on I still have more than double that space left in the cockpit.

I don't want to, but I might have to be creative here to make it like what we see in the movie. Has anyone else come up against this?
